Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Slaughter Purifies Hides of Non-Edible Animals
Hanafi ruling on tadhkiyah purifying hides of non-edible animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of proper Islamic slaughter on the hide and meat of non-edible animals, and identify the conditions that make the slaughter 'shar'iyyah'.

Core Idea
Islamic slaughter purifies the hide of non-edible animals like tanning, but not the meat.

Proper Islamic slaughter (tadhkiyah) is a powerful purifier. This lesson explores its effect on hides of animals whose meat is not permissible to eat. The Hanafi school draws a distinction between the hide and the meat: slaughter purifies the hide for use, but the meat remains impure. This ruling is based on the need for leather and the principle that slaughter works like tanning, even more effectively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage deals with tadhkiyah (Islamic slaughter) and its effect on the hide of ghayr al-ma'kūl (non-edible animals). The ruling is that it purifies the hide, making it permissible to use.
The hide becomes pure (tāhir) for use, e.g., making leather items.
2
List the conditions for shar'iyyah
The slaughter must be 'shar'iyyah': performed by a Muslim or Kitabi (Jew/Christian), with the basmalah recited, not by a Magian, not a pilgrim in ihram hunting, and not omitting the basmalah intentionally.
If any of these conditions is violated, the slaughter does not purify.
3
Understand the analogy to tanning
The author compares slaughter to tanning in that both remove impure moisture. Slaughter is even more effective because it prevents the moisture from entering the hide, while tanning removes it after contamination.
This is a qiyas awwala (a fortiori analogy).
4
Distinguish hide from meat
The text explicitly states that slaughter does not purify the meat (dūna laḥmihi). There are two transmissions (tasʻīḥān) on this, but the most correct view is that meat and fat remain impure.
The need for hide is cited as the reason for its purification, while there is no similar need for the meat of non-edible animals.
5
Note the exception of pig
Pig is excluded from this ruling because it is intrinsically impure (najis al-ʻayn) and cannot be purified by slaughter or tanning.
This exception is carried over from the general rule of impurity of pig.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وتطهر الذكاة الشرعية خرج بها ذبح المجوسي شيئاً، والمحرم صيداً، وتارك التسمية عمداً (جلد غير المأكول) سوى الخنزير لعمل الذكاة عمل الدباغة في إزالة الرطوبات النجسة، بل أولى دون لحمه) فلا يظهر على أصح ما يفنى به من التصحيحين المختلفين في طهارة لحم غير المأكول وشحمه بالذكاة الشرعية للاحتياج إلى الجلد
And proper slaughter (tadhkiyah)—excluding the slaughter of a Magian, a pilgrim hunting in ihram, and one who deliberately omits the basmalah—purifies the hide of a non-edible animal except the pig, because slaughter acts like tanning in removing impure moisture, rather it is more effective. But it does not purify its meat, according to the most correct of the two recensions differing on the purity of meat and fat of non-edible animals by proper slaughter, due to the need for the hide.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling on the effect of ritual slaughter (tadhkiyah) on the hides of non-edible animals. The text establishes that proper Islamic slaughter—performed by a Muslim or kitabi, excluding slaughter by a Magian, a pilgrim in ihram hunting, or one who intentionally omits the basmalah—purifies the hide of non-edible animals (i.e., those whose meat is not eaten) just as tanning does, and even more effectively (بل أولى). The reason is that slaughter prevents the entry of impure moisture into the hide by draining the blood, whereas tanning removes impurities after they have already contaminated the hide. However, the meat itself remains impure and is not purified by slaughter. The commentary mentions that there are two different transmissions (tas'hihan) regarding the status of the meat and fat of non-edible animals: the most correct position is that they are not purified. The reason given for purifying the hide is the human need for leather. The exception of pig is carried over from the previous discussion—pig is intrinsically impure and not purified either by tanning or slaughter.

Key Terms
الذكاة الشرعية (al-tadhkiyah al-shar'iyyah): Slaughter performed according to Islamic law, draining the blood from an animal.
غير المأكول (ghayr al-ma'kūl): Animals whose meat is not permissible to eat, but their hide may be purified for use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effect of proper Islamic slaughter on the hide of a non-edible animal?
A) It purifies both the hide and the meat.
B) It purifies the hide but not the meat.
C) It does not purify either the hide or the meat.
D) It purifies the meat but not the hide.

Key Takeaway
Islamic slaughter purifies the hide of non-edible animals for use, but leaves the meat impure.

Taharah — Purification

Parts That Remain Pure After Death: Hair, Wool, Bone, etc.
Ruling on animal parts that remain pure after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the animal parts that remain pure after death and state the condition that preserves their purity.

Core Idea
Hair, wool, horn, hoof, and bone stay pure after death because blood does not circulate in them.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that a carcass (maytah) becomes impure due to trapped blood. However, certain parts of the animal lack blood circulation, so they remain pure even after death. This lesson identifies those parts and the conditions for their purity, which is important for practical rulings on usage of animal products like wool and bones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Understand that impurity in a dead animal is caused by blood retention (ihtibas al-dam). Parts with no circulating blood are exempt from this impurity.
The principle is based on the idea that blood carries najasah (impurity) after death.
2
List the Exempted Parts
Memorize the parts mentioned: hair (sha'r), wool (suf), horn (qarn), hoof (hafir), and bone ('azm) — provided there is no fat (dasm) on the bone.
The text specifies 'sheared wool' (al-majzuz) as an example.
3
Note the Exceptions
Recognize that the pig (khinzir) is excluded entirely — all its parts are impure. Also, fat on bone is considered impure because it is part of the carcass's fluid.
The fat is impure, but the bone itself remains pure once the fat is removed.
4
Apply the Ruling
In practice, if you encounter a bone from a dead animal, check for attached fat. If clean, it is pure and can be used; if fatty, remove the fat and use the bone.
Similarly, sheared wool from a dead sheep is pure and can be used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وكل شيء) من أجزاء الحيوان غير الخنزير لا يسري فيه الدم لا ينجس بالموت) لأن النجاسة باحتباس الدم، وهو منعدم فيما هو (كالشعر والريش المجزوز) لأن المنسول جدره نجس والقرن والحافر والعظم ما لم يكن به أي العظم (دسم) أي ودك لأنه نجس من الميتة فإذا
And everything from the parts of an animal other than the pig in which blood does not circulate does not become impure by death, because impurity is caused by retention of blood, which is absent in things like hair and sheared wool—because what is plucked is impure—and horn, hoof, and bone, unless there is in it (the bone) fat (dasm), i.e., grease, because it is impure from the carcass.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling enumerating parts of animals that remain pure after death, provided they are free of blood and fat. The general principle is that impurity in a carcass results from blood trapped in the body after death. Parts that do not circulate blood—such as hair, wool, horns, hooves, and bones—do not become impure when the animal dies. However, if a bone has fat or grease on it, that fat is considered impure because it came from the carcass. Therefore, the bone itself is pure, but the fat must be removed. Wool that is already sheared (majnūn) is included because it is detached and does not contain blood. The mention of pig is an exception: all parts of pig are intrinsically impure. This ruling is a memorization anchor for students because it lists specific items that avoid the general impurity of dead animals.

Key Terms
لا يسري فيه الدم (lā yasrī fīhi al-dam): Blood does not circulate in these parts; they are not considered 'living' parts that trap blood upon death.
دسم (dasm): Fat or grease that may be attached to a bone; it is considered impure if from a carcass.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following animal parts does NOT become impure upon death?
A) The blood
B) The hair
C) The fat on bone
D) The flesh

Key Takeaway
Hair, wool, horn, hoof, and bone without fat remain pure after death; fat from carcass is impure.

Taharah — Purification

6 min
Purification of Non-Edible Animal Hides by Shari'i Slaughter
Explaining that shari'i slaughter purifies the hide of non-edible animals except pig, using qiyas on tanning and a divine barrier analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why shari'i slaughter purifies the hide of a non-edible animal (except pig) and identify the qiyas used to derive this ruling.

Core Idea
Shari'i slaughter purifies hide by preventing impure fluid connection, surpassing tanning.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a key question: does shari'i slaughter purify the hide of a non-edible animal? The matn and commentary establish that it does, and even better than tanning, but only the hide—not the meat or fat. The reasoning uses qiyas on tanning, with a difference in mechanism: slaughter prevents impure fluids from reaching the hide, while tanning removes them after they have entered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the explicit ruling: the hide of a non-edible animal (except pig) is purified by shari'i slaughter.
The ruling is based on istihsan and the need for hides.
2
Locate the Proof: Qiyas on Tanning
The proof is a qiyas: tanning purifies the hide of a dead animal by removing impure fluids; slaughter does so even more effectively by preventing those fluids from entering.
The hadith 'Any hide that is tanned is pure' supports the asl.
3
Analyze the Illa (Effective Cause)
The common illa is the removal of impure fluids. In tanning, removal occurs after connection (ba'd al-ittisal); in slaughter, prevention occurs before connection, making slaughter superior.
The barrier between meat and hide prevents fluid transfer during life, analogous to the barrier between blood and milk.
4
Identify Exceptions and Limitations
The hide of a pig is excluded (sawa al-khinzir). Additionally, the meat and fat are NOT purified by slaughter because they were impure during life and remain so.
This differs from the Shafi'i position where all parts become pure.
5
Understand the Critical Refinement
The commentator prefers the 'barrier' explanation over the 'need for hide' explanation for why only the hide is purified, because the barrier is a consistent divine sign while need varies.
This refinement strengthens the analogy to tanning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجزاء الآدمي وتطهر الذكاة الشرعية خرج بها ذبح المجوسي شيئاً، والمحرم صيداً، وتارك التسمية عمداً (جلد غير المأكول) سوى الخنزير لعمل الذكاة عمل الدباغة في إزالة الرطوبات النجسة، بل أولى دون لحمه) فلا يظهر على أصح ما يفنى به من التصحيحين المختلفين في طهارة لحم غير المأكول وشحمه بالذكاة الشرعية للاحتياج إلى الجلد

قوله: (وتطهر الذكاة) هي في اللغة الذبح، وفي الشرع تسييل الدم النجس مطلقاً كما في صيد المبسوط وذكاة الضرورة قسم من التذكية كما في القهستاني قوله: (الشرعية) نقل في البحر من كتاب الطهارة عن الدراية والمجتبى والقنية أن ذبح المجوسي، وتارك التسمية عمداً يوجب الطهارة على الأصح وإن لم يؤكل، وأفاد في التنوير أن اشتراط الذكاة الشرعية هو الأظهر، وان صحح المقابل . قوله : (بل (أولى لأنها تمنع إتصال الرطوبات النجسة والدباغة تزيلها بعد الإتصال لفساد البنية بالموت فأما قبله فكل شيء بمحله، وجعل الله تعالى بين اللحم، والجلد حاجزاً كما جعل بين الدم واللبن حاجزاً حتى خرج طاهراً، أفاده في الشرح قوله: (دون لحمه) لأن حرمة لحمه لا لكرامته آية نجاسته واللحم نجس حال الحياة، فكذا بعد الذكاة. قوله : (للاحتياج إلى الجلد) علة لطهارة الجلد بالذكاة دون غيره والأولى التعليل بوجود الحاجز بين الجلد واللحم كما قدمناه عنه لأنه قد تقع الحاجة للشحم لنحو استصباح.
Parts of a human are purified by shari'i slaughter, excluding the slaughter of a Magian, a muhrim hunting, and one who deliberately omits the basmalah. The hide of a non-edible animal, except pig, because slaughter acts like tanning in removing impure fluids, rather it is better, but not its meat. So it does not appear on the most authentic of the two corrections that differ on the purity of the meat and fat of a non-edible animal by shari'i slaughter due to the need for the hide.
He said: (And purification by slaughter) is in language slaughter, and in Shari'a the flowing of impure blood absolutely as in Sayd al-Mabsut, and emergency slaughter is a type of tathkiyah as in al-Qahistani. He said: (Shari'i) It is narrated in al-Bahr from Kitab al-Tahara from al-Diraya, al-Mujtaba, and al-Qunyah that the slaughter of a Magian and one who deliberately omits the basmalah necessitates purity on the most authentic view even if not eaten, and it is stated in al-Tanwir that requiring shari'i slaughter is the most apparent, and the opposite is corrected. He said: (Rather it is better because it prevents the connection of impure fluids, while tanning removes them after connection due to corruption of the structure by death. As for before [death], everything is in its place. Allah has placed a barrier between meat and skin just as He placed a barrier between blood and milk so that it comes out pure, as mentioned in the commentary. He said: (But not its meat) because the prohibition of its meat is not due to its honor but due to its impurity, and meat is impure during life, so likewise after slaughter. He said: (Due to the need for the hide) is the cause for the purity of the hide by slaughter unlike other parts, and the better explanation is the existence of the barrier between the hide and meat as we have previously mentioned, because there may be a need for fat for something like lighting.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya explaining the effect of shari'i slaughter (tathkiyah) on the hide of non-edible animals. The matn states that slaughter purifies the hide, and even does so more effectively than tanning, but it does not purify the meat. The hashya clarifies that tathkiyah, in Shari'a, means the flowing of impure blood, and it includes emergency slaughter. The condition of shari'i slaughter is discussed: the slaughter of a Magian or one who omits the basmalah intentionally still purifies on the most authentic view. The reason is that slaughter prevents the connection of impure fluids to the skin, while tanning only removes them after they have entered, so slaughter is superior. A divine barrier between skin and meat is cited, similar to the barrier between blood and milk. The meat itself remains impure because it was impure during life, and slaughter does not change that. The need for the hide is the reason for this special ruling, though the commentator prefers the explanation of the barrier.

Key Terms
الذكاة (al-tathkiyah): In language: slaughter. In Shari'a: the flowing of impure blood absolutely, including emergency slaughter.
الدباغة (al-dibagh): The process of tanning a hide to remove impure moisture and purify it.
الجلد (al-jild): The hide or skin of an animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following animals' hides can be purified by shari'i slaughter?
A) Cow (edible animal)
B) Fox (non-edible animal)
C) Pig
D) Human

Key Takeaway
Shari'i slaughter purifies the hide of non-edible animals (except pig) by preventing impure fluids, but the meat and fat remain impure.

Parts Not Becoming Impure Upon Death
Identifying body parts that remain pure after an animal's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which parts of a dead animal are pure according to the Hanafi school and explain the basis in the hadith and the intra-Hanafi disputes on the nerve and milk/rennet.

Core Idea
Parts without life or blood flow remain pure after death — the ruling is based on the hadith that only meat is prohibited.

In the Hanafi school, not everything from a dead animal becomes impure. This lesson examines which parts are exempt, the proof from the hadith, and the intra-Hanafi differences on the nerve and on milk and rennet. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for matters of taharah in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage states that any part of an animal (excluding pig) in which blood does not circulate does not become impure by death. Impurity is linked to the retention of blood after death.
This applies to parts that never had life, like hair and wool.
2
List the explicitly mentioned pure parts
The text lists: hair, plucked wool, horn, hoof, bone (without adherent fat), beak, claw, eggshell, milk, and rennet. Each is considered pure because it does not contain life that ceases.
The hadith from al-Daraqutni supports this: only meat is prohibited.
3
Analyze the proof from hadith
The hadith explicitly exempts hide, hair, and wool from the prohibition of the dead animal. This indicates that these parts are not impure. The Hanafi school generalizes this to all such parts.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
4
Examine the dispute on the nerve
The nerve is considered impure in one narration because it seems to have life (pain when cut). However, the refutation states that pain is due to adjacency to flesh, not inherent life. The relied-upon view is that the nerve is pure.
This illustrates critical refinement within the school.
5
Distinguish the dispute on milk and rennet
Abu Hanifa holds that milk and rennet do not become contaminated (mutanajjis) by death because death does not dissolve them. The Sahibayn say they become contaminated by adjacency to impure membranes, but solid rennet can be washed. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل شيء من أجزاء الحيوان غير الخنزير لا يسري فيه الدم لا ينجس بالموت لأن النجاسة باحتباس الدم، وهو منعدم فيما هو كالشعر والريش المجزوز لأن المنسول جدره نجس والقرن والحافر والعظم ما لم يكن به أي العظم دسم لأنه ودك لأنه نجس من الميتة فإذا زال عن العظم زال عنه النجس، والعظم في ذاته طاهر لما أخرج الدارقطني إنما حرم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من الميتة لحمها فأما الجلد والشعر والصوف فلا بأس به والعصب نجس في الصحيح من الرواية لأن فيه حياة بدليل التألم بقطعه ، وقيل : طاهر لأنه عظم غير صلب

قوله: (لا يسري فيه الدم الخ) أفاد المصنف أن الطهارة لعدم وجود الدم في هذه الأشياء وهو الذي في غاية البيان، والذي في الهداية أن عدم نجاسة هذه الأشياء بسبب أنها ليست بميتة لأن الميتة من الحيوانات في عرف الشرع إسم لما زالت حياته لا يصنع من العباد أو بصنع غير مشروع، ولا حياة في هذه الأشياء فلا تكون نجسة .اهـ. قوله: (كالشعر الخ) والمنقار والمخلب وبيضة ضعيفة القشرة ولبن وإنفحة وهي ما يكون في معدة الجدي، ونحوه الرضيع من أجزاء اللبن قبل أن يأكل. قال في الفتح : لا خلاف بين أصحابنا في ذلك، وإنما الخلاف من حيث تنجسهما، فقالا : نعم لمجاورتهما الغشاء النجس، فإن كانت الأنفحة جامدة تظهر بالغسل، وإلا تعذر تطهيرها كاللبن، وقال أبو حنيفة ليستا بمتنجستين لأن الموت لا يحلهما، وشمل كلامه السن لأنها أعظم طاهر، وهو ظاهر المذهب، ورواية نجاستها شاذة كما في الحموي على الأشياء، وعدم جواز الإنتفاع به حيث قالوا: لو طعن في دقيق لا يؤكل لتعظيمه لا لنجاسته قوله : (ما لم يكن به أي العظم) لو أعاد الضمير إلى كل المذكور قبله لكان أولى. قوله : (لأنه نجس) أي الودك، وقوله من الميتة أي من أجزائها فإذا وجد على نحو العظم ينجسه، ويطهر بإزالته عنه 

قوله: (بدليل التألم بقطعه) ردّه في مجمع الأنهر بأن التألم الحاصل فيه للمجاورة والإتصال باللحم، ويلزم هذا القائل أن يقول بنجاسة العظم أيضاً لأنه يتألم بكسره ولا قائل به.
And every part of an animal other than pig in which blood does not flow does not become impure by death, because impurity is due to the retention of blood, and it is absent in what is like hair and plucked wool, because what is spun its hide is impure, and the horn, hoof, and bone as long as there is no fat on the bone, because fat is impure from a dead body, then if it [the fat] is removed from the bone, the impurity is removed from it, and the bone itself is pure based on what al-Daraqutni reported: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) only prohibited the meat of the dead animal; as for the hide, hair, and wool, there is no harm.' And the nerve is impure in the correct narration because it contains life, evidence by the pain in cutting it, and it is said: pure because it is a bone not hard.

He said: ('No blood flows in it' etc.) The author indicated that purity is due to the absence of blood in these things, which is very clear. And what is in al-Hidayah is that these things are not impure because they are not a dead body; for a dead animal in the custom of Shari'a is a name for what has lost life due to an act of worship or an unlegislated act, and there is no life in these things, so they are not impure. end. He said: ('Like hair' etc.) And the beak, claw, egg with a weak shell, milk, and rennet which is in the stomach of a kid and similar suckling from parts of milk before it eats. He said in al-Fath: There is no difference among our companions in that; rather the difference is regarding their becoming contaminated. So they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Yes, due to their adjacency to the impure membrane; if the rennet is solid, it becomes clean by washing, otherwise it is difficult to purify like milk. And Abu Hanifa said: They are not mutanajjis because death does not dissolve them. And his speech includes the tooth because it is a pure bone, and this is the apparent madhhab, and the narration of its impurity is irregular as in al-Hamawi on the things, and the impermissibility of benefiting from it where they said: If it is ground into flour, it is not eaten not because of impurity but because of respect. He said: ('As long as there is no fat on the bone') If he had returned the pronoun to everything mentioned before, it would have been better. He said: ('Because it is impure') i.e., the fat, and his saying 'from a dead body' i.e., from its parts, so if it is found on something like bone, it makes it impure, and it is purified by removing it.

He said: ('Evidence by the pain in cutting it') It was refuted in Majma' al-Anhur that the pain that occurs is due to adjacency and connection to the flesh, and this speaker would have to say that the bone is also impure because it feels pain when broken, and no one says that.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya discusses the parts of an animal that do not become impure upon death. The matn states that any part in which blood does not circulate—such as hair, wool, horns, hooves, and bones (unless they have adherent fat)—remains pure. The proof is the hadith from al-Daraqutni that only meat is prohibited from a dead animal; hide, hair, and wool are permissible. The nerve (asab) is considered impure in the correct narration because it has life evidenced by pain upon cutting, but a minority view says it is pure. The hashya elaborates that the Hidayah explains impurity is due to retention of blood, so these parts are not impure. It then addresses a dispute: whether milk and rennet from a dead animal become contaminated (mutanajjis) due to contact with impure tissue. Abu Hanifa holds they are not contaminable because death does not dissolve them, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say they are contaminated if adjacent to impure membranes, but can be purified by washing if solid. The hashya also clarifies that fat from a dead animal is impure and contaminates the bone it adheres to, but the bone itself is pure. Finally, the refutation of the nerve's impurity is mentioned: pain is due to connection to flesh, not inherent life, so the nerve is pure. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute with the preferred view being that nerve and these parts are not impure.

Key Terms
الميتة (al-maytah): A dead animal; in Shari'a, what has lost life due to an unlegislated act or not slaughtered properly.
العصب (al-asab): The nerve or tendon; in this passage, it is discussed whether it contains life and thus becomes impure upon death.
الأنفحة (al-infahah): Rennet, a substance found in the stomach of a suckling animal, used to curdle milk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the nerve (asab) of a dead animal?
A) It is impure because it has life.
B) It is pure because pain is due to adjacency to flesh.
C) It is impure only if it has fat.
D) The nerve is not discussed in the passage.

Key Takeaway
Parts without blood flow or life remain pure after death; the nerve is pure on the relied-upon view, and the general principle is confirmed by the hadith that only meat is prohibited.

Purity of Musk, Musk Pod, and Civet
Declaring purity of musk, pod, civet; permissibility of eating musk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of musk, its pod, and civet, and explain the role of istihalah (transformation) as a purifier.

Core Idea
Musk and civet are pure because istihalah transforms their impure origins into lawful substances.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the Hanafi school on the purity of musk, its pod (nafijah), and civet. The text declares them absolutely pure and musk lawful to eat, based on consensus and the principle of istihalah—transformation of an impure substance into a pure one. The commentary clarifies nuances about the pod's contact with water and the scope of tanning, reinforcing the centrality of istihalah as a purifier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The passage rules on three items: musk (misk), its pod (nafijah), and civet (zabad). The ruling is that they are pure (tahir) and musk is lawful (halal) to eat.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The primary proof is ijma (consensus) on the purity of musk, as indicated by the phrase 'due to consensus on its purity' (للإتفاق على طهارته). The secondary basis is the principle of istihalah, which is a purifier.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the consensus prove the ruling? The consensus of scholars is qat'i (definitive) in transmission and meaning, establishing the ruling with certainty. The principle of istihalah explains why musk, originally from blood, becomes pure.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi clarification
The text addresses an issue: whether the musk pod is pure if it spoils when water contacts it. The author clarifies that the pod is pure absolutely, even if from a dead animal, and that it does not revert to impurity—paralleling legal tanning.
This counters a potential misunderstanding that impurity might return.
5
Evaluate the role of istihalah
The hashya explicitly states that istihalah is a purifier (مطهرة). This principle allows substances that undergo complete transformation (e.g., blood to musk, wine to vinegar) to be ruled pure. It is the underlying rationale for the ruling.
Istihalah is a well-established usul principle in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونافجة المسك طاهرة مطلقاً ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء كما تقدم في الدباغة الحكمية (كالمسك) للإتفاق على طهارته (وأكله) أي المسك (حلال) ونص على حل أكله لأنه لا يلزم من طهارة الشيء حل أكله كالتراب طاهر لا يحل أكله (والزباد) معروف (طاهر نصح صلاة متطيب به لإستحالته للطيبية كالمسك فإنه بعض دم الغزال وقد اتفق على طهارته، وليس إلا بالإستحالة للطيبية والإستحالة مطهرة والله تعالى الموفق بمنه وكرمه.

قوله: (ونافجة المسك) بالجيم والفاء المفتوحة كما في أكثر كتب اللغة الجلدة التي يجتمع فيها المسك. قوله: (ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء) الأولى ولا تفسد بإصابة الماء، وقوله مطلقاً يفسر بأنها سواء كانت من ذكية، أو ميتة، أو انفصلت من حية . قوله : (كما تقدم في الدباغة الحكمية) لم يقدمه على أن هذا خلاف المنصوص فإنه تقدم عن السراج أنه يشترط عدم عود الفساد إلى الجلد عند حصول الماء فيه، والذي في الشرح، وقد علمت حكم الدباغة الحكمية وعدم العود إلى النجاسة بإصابة الماء على الصحيح اهـ وهو الأولى وأوقعه في هذا الإيهام الاختصار، وتبعه السيد في الشرح قوله: (وأكله حلال) ولو من حيوان غير مذكي، ولأكله فوائد ذكرها صاحب القاموس فارجع إليها إن رمتها . قوله : (والزياد) كسحاب كما في القاموس قوله : (معروف) هو وسخ يجتمع تحت ذنب السنور على المخرج فتمسك الدابة وتمنع الاضطراب ويسلت الوسخ هنالك بليطة، أو بخرقة قاموس.
And the musk pod is absolutely pure, even if it would spoil by the contact of water, as previously mentioned in the case of legal tanning (like musk) due to consensus on its purity. And its eating, i.e., musk, is lawful. It is explicitly stated that it is lawful to eat because the purity of a thing does not necessitate its lawfulness, like dust is pure but not lawful to eat. And civet, well-known, is pure. It is correct to pray while perfumed with it due to its transformation into a pure substance, like musk, for it is part of the blood of a deer and there is consensus on its purity. And it is only due to transformation into a pure substance, and transformation is a purifier. And Allah is the Granter of success by His grace and generosity.

He said: (The musk pod) with jim and fatha as in most language books: the skin in which musk collects. He said: (Even if it would spoil by contact of water) rather, it does not spoil by contact of water. And his saying 'absolutely' is interpreted to mean whether it comes from a slaughtered animal, a dead one, or is separated from a live one. He said: (As previously mentioned in legal tanning) he did not mention it, but this is contrary to the stated text, for it was mentioned from al-Siraj that it is required that the skin does not return to spoilage when water reaches it. And what is in the commentary: you have known the ruling of legal tanning and that it does not return to impurity by contact of water on the correct view. end. And it is better, and this ambiguity was caused by brevity. And the sayyid followed him in the commentary. He said: (And its eating is lawful) even from a non-slaughtered animal. And it has benefits mentioned by the author of al-Qamus, so refer to them if you wish. He said: (And civet) like a cloud as in al-Qamus. He said: (Well-known) it is the dirt that collects under the tail of a cat at the anus, then the animal is restrained and prevented from disturbance, and the dirt is removed there with a cloth or a rag. Qamus.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage rules on the purity of musk (misk), its pod (nafijah), and civet (zabad). The matn declares them absolutely pure, even if the pod would spoil by contact with water, by analogy with legal tanning. There is consensus on their purity. Musk is also lawful to eat, but the hashya notes that purity does not necessarily imply edibility (cf. dust). Civet is also pure; one may pray while perfumed with it because it has undergone istihalah (transformation) from an impure origin (blood or waste) into a pure substance. The hashya explains that the musk pod is the skin containing musk, and its purity applies regardless of whether the animal was slaughtered, dead, or alive. The reference to tanning is clarified: the correct view is that once tanned, the skin does not revert to impurity when water contacts it. Eating musk is permissible even from a non-slaughtered animal, due to transformation. The principle is that istihalah (transformation) is a purifier.

Key Terms
المسك (al-misk): Musk, a perfume derived from a gland of the musk deer; here ruled pure and halal.
النافجة (al-nafijah): The skin (pod) that contains musk.
الإستحالة (al-istihalah): Transformation of a substance from an impure state to a pure one, e.g., blood turning into musk, or wine turning into vinegar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the Shafi'i school says so.

Key Takeaway
Musk and civet are pure and edible due to istihalah, which is a purifier in the Hanafi school.

The Bone of a Dead Animal is Pure
Ruling on the purity of bones from dead animals with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the bone of a dead animal and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The bone of a dead animal is pure because the Prophet only forbade the meat.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the bone of a dead animal is pure. The key evidence is a hadith from al-Daraqutni. Understanding this distinction helps in practical purity issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The bone of a dead animal is ruled pure (tahir).
This is not the same as the impurity of the meat.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from al-Daraqutni: the Prophet only forbade the meat, so other parts are not automatically impure.
3
Understand the condition
Once external impurity (blood) is removed, the bone is pure.
The bone itself is not inherently impure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زال عن العظم زال عنه النجس، والعظم في ذاته طاهر لما أخرج الدارقطني إنما حرم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من الميتة لحمها فأما الجلد والشعر والصوف فلا بأس به والعصب نجس في الصحيح من الرواية لأن فيه حياة بدليل التألم بقطعه ، وقيل : طاهر لأنه عظم غير صلب (ونافجة المسك طاهرة) مطلقاً ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء كما تقدم في الدباغة الحكمية (كالمسك) للإتفاق على طهارته (وأكله) أي المسك (حلال) ونص على حل أكله لأنه لا يلزم من طهارة الشيء حل أكله كالتراب طاهر لا يحل أكله (والزباد) معروف (طاهر نصح صلاة متطيب به لإستحالته للطيبية كالمسك فإنه بعض دم الغزال وقد اتفق على طهارته، وليس إلا بالإستحالة للطيبية والإستحالة مطهرة والله تعالى الموفق بمنه وكرمه.
قوله: (بدليل التألم بقطعه) ردّه في مجمع الأنهر بأن التألم الحاصل فيه للمجاورة والإتصال باللحم، ويلزم هذا القائل أن يقول بنجاسة العظم أيضاً لأنه يتألم بكسره ولا قائل به. قوله : (ونافجة المسك) بالجيم والفاء المفتوحة كما في أكثر كتب اللغة الجلدة التي يجتمع فيها المسك. قوله: (ولو كانت تفسد بإصابة الماء) الأولى ولا تفسد بإصابة الماء، وقوله مطلقاً يفسر بأنها سواء كانت من ذكية، أو ميتة، أو انفصلت . من حية .
قوله : (كما تقدم في الدباغة الحكمية) لم يقدمه على أن هذا خلاف المنصوص فإنه تقدم عن السراج أنه يشترط عدم عود الفساد إلى الجلد عند حصول الماء فيه، والذي في الشرح، وقد علمت حكم الدباغة الحكمية وعدم العود إلى النجاسة بإصابة الماء على الصحيح اهـ وهو الأولى وأوقعه في هذا الإيهام الاختصار، وتبعه السيد في الشرح قوله: (وأكله حلال) ولو من حيوان غير مذكي، ولأكله فوائد ذكرها صاحب القاموس فارجع إليها إن رمتها . قوله : (والزياد) كسحاب كما في القاموس قوله : (معروف) هو وسخ يجتمع تحت ذنب السنور على المخرج فتمسك الدابة وتمنع الاضطراب ويسلت الوسخ هنالك بليطة، أو بخرقة قاموس.
When blood is removed from the bone, the impurity is removed, and the bone in itself is pure because al-Daraqutni narrated: The Messenger of Allah (SAW) only forbade the meat of the dead animal, but as for the skin, hair, and wool, there is no problem. The nerve is impure in the correct narration because it has life, evidenced by the pain felt when it is cut, and it is said: it is pure because it is a solid bone. And the musk pouch is absolutely pure, even if it spoils by contact with water, as previously stated in the section on legal tanning. Like musk, there is consensus on its purity. And eating musk is permissible, and it is explicitly stated that its eating is permissible because the purity of a thing does not necessitate that its eating is permissible, just as dust is pure but not permissible to eat. And civet is known and pure, it is permissible to pray perfumed with it because it has transformed into a perfume like musk, for it is part of the blood of the deer, and there is consensus on its purity, and that is only due to transformation into perfume, and transformation is a purifier. May Allah grant success.
His saying: (evidence of pain when cut) is refuted in Majma‘ al-Anhur because the pain that occurs is due to adjacency and connection to the flesh, and this would oblige the one who says this to say that the bone is also impure because it feels pain when broken, but no one says that. His saying: (and the musk pouch) with jim and fa' pronounced with fatha as in most lexicons: the skin in which musk collects. His saying: (even if it spoils by contact with water) the better expression is 'and it does not spoil by contact with water', and his saying 'absolutely' is interpreted as meaning whether it is from a slaughtered animal, a dead animal, or separated from a living one.
His saying: (as previously stated in the section on legal tanning) he did not mention it earlier in a way that this contradicts what is transmitted, for it was mentioned earlier from al-Siraj that it is a condition that the impurity does not return to the skin when water contacts it, and what is in the commentary is: and you have learned the ruling of legal tanning and that it does not revert to impurity by contact with water according to the correct opinion, etc., and it is better, and this misunderstanding is caused by abbreviation, and al-Sayyid followed him in the commentary. His saying: (and its eating is permissible) even if from an animal not slaughtered, and its eating has benefits mentioned by the author of al-Qamus, so refer to them if you desire. His saying: (and civet) like 'sahab' as in al-Qamus. His saying: (known) it is the dirt that collects under the tail of the cat at the excretory opening; the animal stops and prevents disturbance, and the dirt is wiped off there with a piece of leather or a cloth. Qamus.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the base text Maraqi al-Falah. It discusses several rulings related to purity and impurity.

First, it deals with the bone of a dead animal. The correct view is that the bone is pure because the prohibition of consuming a dead animal applies only to its flesh, not to bones, skin, hair, or wool. This is supported by a hadith from al-Daraqutni. When impurity (blood) is removed from the bone, the bone itself becomes pure; it is not inherently impure.

Second, it addresses the nerve. According to the sound transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), the nerve of a dead animal is impure. The reason given is that it contains life, evidenced by the pain felt when cut. However, the commentator refutes this reasoning by stating that the pain is due to the nerve's connection to the flesh, not life within the nerve itself. If pain indicated impurity, a bone would also be impure because it causes pain when broken—but no scholar holds that view. Despite this refutation, the ruling that the nerve is impure remains the relied-upon position.

Third, musk from a musk deer is pure and its eating is halal. The musk pouch (nafajat al-misk) is pure even if it comes from a dead animal or if water damages it. The permissibility of eating musk is distinct from its purity; purity alone does not imply halal consumption, as exemplified by dust which is pure but not edible. The basis for both purity and edibility is the transformation (istihala) of the blood into a pure substance.

Fourth, civet (zabad) is also pure, and it is permissible to pray while perfumed with it. Like musk, it undergoes transformation into a pure perfume.

Finally, the commentator clarifies terms: nafajat al-misk is the pouch in which musk forms; civet is a secretion under the tail of a cat-like animal. The discussion reinforces that istihala (transformation) is a valid purifier in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عظم (azm): Bone of an animal
ميتة (maytah): Dead animal not slaughtered properly

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the bone being pure?
A) Consensus
B) Hadith from al-Daraqutni
C) Qiyas on skin
D) Istihala

Key Takeaway
The bone of a dead animal is pure, based on the Prophetic statement that only the meat is forbidden.
